module GRHO$SYNTAX [org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(116,1,272,9)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/home/isaac/Documents/KFramework/Git/Languages/GroundedRho/./grho.k))]
  imports SUBSTITUTION$SYNTAX
  imports MAP$SYNTAX
  imports GRHO-SYNTAX$SYNTAX
  syntax TuplespaceCellOpt ::= TuplespaceCell
  syntax TuplespaceCellOpt ::= "noTuplespaceCell"
  syntax TuplespaceCellFragment ::= "<tuplespace>-fragment" SendsCellOpt ReceivesCellOpt "</tuplespace>-fragment"
  syntax TuplespaceCell ::= "initTuplespaceCell"
  syntax TuplespaceCell ::= "<tuplespace>" SendsCell ReceivesCell "</tuplespace>"
  syntax TupleCellOpt ::= TupleCell
  syntax TupleCellOpt ::= "noTupleCell"
  syntax TupleCell ::= "initTupleCell"
  syntax TupleCell ::= "<tuple>" K "</tuple>"
  syntax ThreadpoolCellOpt ::= ThreadpoolCell
  syntax ThreadpoolCellOpt ::= "noThreadpoolCell"
  syntax ThreadpoolCellFragment ::= "<threadpool>-fragment" ThreadCellBag "</threadpool>-fragment"
  syntax ThreadpoolCell ::= "initThreadpoolCell" "(" Map ")"
  syntax ThreadpoolCell ::= "<threadpool>" ThreadCellBag "</threadpool>"
  syntax ThreadCellFragment ::= "<thread>-fragment" KCellOpt "</thread>-fragment"
  syntax ThreadCellBag [UNIQUE_ID(ffaf034f111991095c71efbd5df430d825b2406df5aac222d221c1d1c97c0fc7) hook(BAG.Bag)]
  syntax ThreadCellBag ::= ThreadCellBag ThreadCellBag
  syntax ThreadCellBag ::= ThreadCell
  syntax ThreadCellBag ::= "ThreadCellBagItem" "(" ThreadCell ")"
  syntax ThreadCellBag ::= ".ThreadCellBag"
  syntax ThreadCell ::= "initThreadCell" "(" Map ")"
  syntax ThreadCell ::= "<thread>" KCell "</thread>"
  syntax TCellFragment ::= "<T>-fragment" ThreadpoolCellOpt TuplespaceCellOpt "</T>-fragment"
  syntax TCell ::= "initTCell" "(" Map ")"
  syntax TCell ::= "<T>" ThreadpoolCell TuplespaceCell "</T>"
  syntax SendsCellOpt ::= SendsCell
  syntax SendsCellOpt ::= "noSendsCell"
  syntax SendsCellFragment ::= "<sends>-fragment" SendCellBag "</sends>-fragment"
  syntax SendsCell ::= "initSendsCell"
  syntax SendsCell ::= "<sends>" SendCellBag "</sends>"
  syntax SendCellFragment ::= "<send>-fragment" SchanCellOpt MsgCellOpt TupleCellOpt "</send>-fragment"
  syntax SendCellBag [UNIQUE_ID(f36daa721239b6daacb7b807221c0a2d46b014bb953607404cd8d575fe554c85) hook(BAG.Bag)]
  syntax SendCellBag ::= SendCellBag SendCellBag
  syntax SendCellBag ::= SendCell
  syntax SendCellBag ::= "SendCellBagItem" "(" SendCell ")"
  syntax SendCellBag ::= ".SendCellBag"
  syntax SendCell ::= "initSendCell"
  syntax SendCell ::= "<send>" SchanCell MsgCell TupleCell "</send>"

  ModuleComment( \section{User-Defined Lists} It is very common in \K to define a shorthand
   for lists of user-defined sorts. \K 's builtin way of doing this is to use
   List\{KItem,"Separator"\}, where "Separator" is any valid character or
   sequence of characters used to separate distinct elements.
   For example, after defining \\
   syntax KItem ::= Elt\\
   a user could then define
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,","\} \\
   which would be a comma-separated list whose elements are all of sort Elt. A
   user could just as well define \\
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,"and"\} \\
   which would be a list containing elements of sort Elt that are separated with
   the word "and". If only one argument is given, the separator is asumed to be
   commas. So, \\
   syntax Elts = List\{Elt\} \\
   would define a comma-separated list containing elements of sort Elt.

  ModuleComment( \section{Description} \K lists are ordered collections that may contain
   duplicate elements. These behave more like lists in functional programming
   languages than arrays in imperative programming languages; there's no
   numerical indexing, but instead specific elements are refered to using the
   Mylist,Mylist construct in combination with the MyListItem construct. It's
   worth noting that \K lists aren't exactly like lists in functional languages;
   they're associative, which means that it's easy to access elements at both
   ends of the lists and concatenate them. For example, L:Mylist,E accesses
